    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer356736657456640871">Billy Milligan can be anyone he wants to be . . . except himself. <br/><br/>Out of control of his actions, Billy Milligan was a man tormented by twenty-four distinct personalities battling for supremacy over his body—a battle that culminated when he awoke in jail, arrested for the kidnap and rape of three women. In a landmark trial, Billy was acquitted of his crimes by reason of ins</span>
  <span id="freeText356736657456640871" style="display:none">Billy Milligan can be anyone he wants to be . . . except himself. <br /><br />Out of control of his actions, Billy Milligan was a man tormented by twenty-four distinct personalities battling for supremacy over his body—a battle that culminated when he awoke in jail, arrested for the kidnap and rape of three women. In a landmark trial, Billy was acquitted of his crimes by reason of insanity caused by multiple personality—the first such court decision in history—bringing to public light the most remarkable and harrowing case of multiple personality ever recorded.<br /><br />Twenty-four people live inside Billy Milligan. Philip, a petty criminal; Kevin, who dealt drugs and masterminded a drugstore robbery; April, whose only ambition was to kill Billy's stepfather; Adalana, the shy, lonely, affection-starved lesbian who “used” Billy's body in the rapes that led to his arrest; David, the eight-year-old “keeper of pain”; and all of the others, including men, women, several children, both boys and girls, and the Teacher, the only one who can put them all together. You will meet each in this often shocking true story. And you will be drawn deeply into the mind of this tortured young man and his splintered, terrifying world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="356736657456640871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Keyes Himself regularly Interviewed Milligan during his treatment and conferred with his carers. I'm only reading it now but It seems to be a fair por<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Keyes Himself regularly Interviewed Milligan during his treatment and conferred with his carers. I'm only reading it now but It seems to be a fair portrayal. at times shocking but not in a way one might suspect of being overdrawn. Excellent book, would highly suggest if at all interest.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_265600756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265600756" />
    <a title="Frank Tibbetts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7491224-frank-tibbetts"><img alt="Frank Tibbetts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327169104p2/7491224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/265600756?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frank Tibbetts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frank Tibbetts" href="/user/show/7491224-frank-tibbetts">Frank Tibbetts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553263817" href="/book/show/112504.The_Minds_of_Billy_Milligan">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265600756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11192851539097320250">Author Daniel Keyes has presented a very riveting description of the human condition if it is pushed too far. I have read this book twice and I have to say that it is one of the best books I have ever read. <br/>Enduring unbelievably cruel tortures as a child at the hands of his stepfather, including sodomy and being forced to dig his own grave-and yes, being buried alive in that same grave, Billy Milligan's mind fragmented into 24 seperate and distinct personalities. I have posted the alter ego's be</span>
  <span id="freeText11192851539097320250" style="display:none">Author Daniel Keyes has presented a very riveting description of the human condition if it is pushed too far. I have read this book twice and I have to say that it is one of the best books I have ever read. <br />Enduring unbelievably cruel tortures as a child at the hands of his stepfather, including sodomy and being forced to dig his own grave-and yes, being buried alive in that same grave, Billy Milligan's mind fragmented into 24 seperate and distinct personalities. I have posted the alter ego's below from this book, so that the potential reader can see how fantastic, and at the same time, how horrifying this man's condition was at the time of his arrest for several campus rapes, which he claimed he had no rememberance of committing. <br />1. Billy Milligan (William Stanley Milligan) is the core personality. <br />2. Arthur is a sophisticated Englishman. He is an expert in science and medicine. He is in "the spot when intellectual thinking is required. <br />3. Ragen Vadascovinich is the "keeper of hate". Ragen is Yugoslavian, has a Slavic accent and he can write and speak in Serbo-Croatian. He controls the spot when danger is immenent. <br />4. Allen is a con man and a manipulator. He is the most common person to talk to the outside world. He plays the drums and paints portraits. Also the only right-handed self. He is the only personality that smokes cigarettes. <br />5. Tommy is the escape artist; he is often confused with Allen. He plays the tenor sax and is an electronics expert. He is also a painter, specializing in landscapes. <br />6. Danny is afraid of people, especially men. He only paints still lifes, saying that this was because Chalmer made him dig his own grave and buried him in it. <br />7. David, age eight, is the "keeper of pain". He comes to the spot to take the pain of the others. <br />8. Christene, age three, was the one who would stand in the corner in school when "Billy" would get in trouble. She has dyslexia, but Arthur taught her to read and write. Ragen has a special bond with her. <br />9. Christopher, Christene's brother, plays the harmonica. <br />10. Adalana, a lesbian, cooks and cleans house for the others, and writes poetry. Milligan's attorney claimed that Adalana had admitted to committing the rapes without the knowledge of Milligan or the other alters <br />11. Phil is a thug and took part in planning some small time crimes. Has a Brooklyn accent. Marked due to him being a criminal. <br />12. Kevin is a criminal planner; he helped devise a plan to rob a drug store. Labeled also because he is a criminal. <br />13. Walter is Australian. He calls himself a big-game hunter and has an excellent sense of direction. Was often used as a spotter. He was labeled because he shot and killed a crow. <br />14. April only has thoughts about destroying Billy's stepfather. Declared an Undesirable when she convinced Ragen to kill Chalmer. Luckily though Arthur was able to talk him out of it at the last second. <br />15. Samual is the Jewish person. He is the only one who believes in God. Was marked because he sold some of the other people's personal paintings. <br />16. Mark is the workhorse. He is often referred to as the zombie because he does nothing unless he is told, and will stare at walls when bored. <br />17. Steve is the impostor, he uses imitations for comedy. Steve never accepted that he was an MP. He was made to be undesirable because his comedy caused the family problems. <br />18. Lee is the prankster and his practical jokes normally get the family into trouble. He does not care about consequences for his actions. He was made an undesirable because one of his jokes put them into solitary confinement. <br />19. Jason is the pressure valve. He was used at the beginning to release tension for the family, but he caused them to get into too much trouble and was marked as an undesirable. <br />20. Bobby always dreams of leading some adventure or fixing some global crisis, but he has no ambitions and was labeled due to that fact. <br />21. Shawn, who is four and deaf, makes buzzing sounds so he can feel the vibration in his head. He was labeled an undesirable because there was no benefit from being deaf later on in life. (Even though he is an undesirable he was never cast into the shadows beyond the spot; he was just never allowed to take the spot.) <br />22. Martin is a snob, from New York. He wants things just handed over to him without earning them. <br />23. Timothy worked in a florist shop until he encountered a homosexual who flirted with him. He went into his own world after that. <br />The Teacher <br />24. (Note: the teacher is not an Undesirable.) The Teacher, was by far the greatest milestone to helping Billy achieve fusion. He is the sum of all other 23 people put together, and has almost total recall of all the other people's actions and thoughts. <br />There are several pictures in this novel of exquisitely detailed paintings his personalities created while he was incarcerated that simply dumb-founds me. <br />I like this book because it is REAL. I strongly recommend this book to anyone who has ever wondered how far the human mind will go to protect itself.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11192851539097320250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4881781519842689383">I read this book in 1988 as I have always been fascinated with 'split personalities' and the fact that this is a local story (based in Ohio... Milligan even spent time in Zanesville and was treated in Columbus). Daniel Keyes does a fantastic job of introducing the reader to all of Milligan's personalities and helping you understand what daily life was like for Milligan.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer892702331901428406">This book is a serious mind fuck for me.<br/><br/>When it comes to writing technique; this book lacks of dramatic elements, and the language used is too clinical, too many characters, and probably the conversations in the book were transcribed from tapes. But once I took the book, I was drawn so deeply by the story.<br/><br/>The details I found in this book put me in amazement. I could see each characters' description clearly and fell in love with Allen (and so were my friends). I sympathized each people inside Bil</span>
  <span id="freeText892702331901428406" style="display:none">This book is a serious mind fuck for me.<br /><br />When it comes to writing technique; this book lacks of dramatic elements, and the language used is too clinical, too many characters, and probably the conversations in the book were transcribed from tapes. But once I took the book, I was drawn so deeply by the story.<br /><br />The details I found in this book put me in amazement. I could see each characters' description clearly and fell in love with Allen (and so were my friends). I sympathized each people inside Billy. Almost a heartbreaking that he still could survive within the condition and hard life. His life story is completely absorbing. I couldn't help but wondering "who am I staring at?" whenever I see his photos. Billy Milligan put me in hours googling for MPD cases and even more hours discussing it with friends. I have a big interest in human mind and psychology, and this book is a full course for me.<br /><br />Billy and this book are inspiration.</span>

  <span id="freeText16327309062065614069" style="display:none"><b>Failed to keep it concise and to the point</b><br />Having obscured the story with countless irrelevant details, Daniel Keyes succeeded in exasperating at least one of his readers. Who cares if Billy's case manager has started hunting deer annually since she was twelve? I thought the title of this book was <i>The Minds of Billy Milligan</i>. My only reason for giving it three stars is that I appreciate the tremendous effort Keyes put into conducting proper research for his book, albeit I am not convinced none of the information he extracted from the interviews with William Milligan wasn't opinionated at all.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2142146743" />
    <a title="Jackdaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21764381-jackdaw"><img alt="Jackdaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605916454p2/21764381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2142146743?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackdaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackdaw" href="/user/show/21764381-jackdaw">Jackdaw</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21764381-jackdaw?shelf=autobiography-biography-memoir">autobiography-biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21764381-jackdaw?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21764381-jackdaw?shelf=sucker-punch">sucker-punch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21764381-jackdaw?shelf=%CF%80%CE%BF%CE%BD%CE%AC%CF%89_%CF%80%CE%B9%CE%BF_%CF%80%CE%BF%CE%BB%CF%8D_%CE%BA-_%CE%B1%CF%80%CF%8C_%CF%84%CE%BF%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B1%CE%BD%CF%84%CE%B5%CE%BB%CE%AF%CE%B4%CE%B7">πονάω_πιο_πολύ_κ-_από_τον_παντελίδη</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21764381-jackdaw?shelf=beyond_compare">beyond_compare</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2142146743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9106375526342525218"><blockquote>
<i>“Do you want someone to write about you, Billy?” Caul asked.<br/><br/>“I guess I could use the money. When I get better and go out into society, I’ll need something to support me. Who would give me a job?”<br/><br/>“Aside from the money, how do you think you’d feel about the whole world reading about your life?”<br/><br/>Billy frowned. <b>“I think people should know. It could help them understand what child abuse can lead to.”<blockquote></blockquote></b></i><br/><br/><blockquote> <pre><br/><br/>Μια ψαλιδιά ένιωσα στο νου<br/>σαν να'χε χωριστεί<br/>έπιασα να το ράψω<br/>μα δεν ταίριαζε η κλωστή.<br/><br/>I felt a cleava</pre></blockquote></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText9106375526342525218" style="display:none"><blockquote>

<div id="review_2007449615" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2007449615" />
    <a title="Luke Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30710594-luke-taylor"><img alt="Luke Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522269800p2/30710594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2007449615?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luke Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luke Taylor" href="/user/show/30710594-luke-taylor">Luke Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2007449615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4470839396905378678">The Minds of Billy Milligan by Daniel Keyes is a challenging look at the controversial case of William Stanley Milligan, a man diagnosed with multiple disorder, who was acquitted for several violent and heinous crimes by pleading insanity as his defense. Armed with sympathetic psychologists and skilled lawyers, the strange case of Billy Milligan is chronicled in great detail by Daniel Keyes, best known for his book, Flowers For Algernon, which also delves deeply into murky waters of human psycho</span>
  <span id="freeText4470839396905378678" style="display:none">The Minds of Billy Milligan by Daniel Keyes is a challenging look at the controversial case of William Stanley Milligan, a man diagnosed with multiple disorder, who was acquitted for several violent and heinous crimes by pleading insanity as his defense. Armed with sympathetic psychologists and skilled lawyers, the strange case of Billy Milligan is chronicled in great detail by Daniel Keyes, best known for his book, Flowers For Algernon, which also delves deeply into murky waters of human psychology. Daniel Keyes’ narrative flair sensationalizes quite a bit at times, making this “nonfiction” piece a tough pill to swallow. No one can argue Billy had a difficult upbringing and endured countless horrors, but Keyes’ narrative liberties in establishing the many voices of the personalities and their names and their characters and their psychological space feels uneasy to read in retrospect, as the account goes into great detail in many places, and yet, the human being that is Milligan offers no recompense to those innocents he has hurt. Where many in the narrative seemingly fall captive to the magical powers of an adept conman, becoming deeply empathetic, negative viewpoints hold much more weight though are few and far between in the book, and feel almost like villainous voices. One of the biggest problems concerning Milligan was the publicity of his case and his trial, and all that came of it should stand as a warning to the legal system of the United States as to keep justice a swift and quiet affair, as committers of violent crimes like Milligan do not deserve any opportunity to become folk heroes or talk show subjects. The press can only make a mess. One can only feel negative emotions throughout the course of reading this, and while I cannot blame Daniel Keyes for his work in covering this story, I cannot compliment him either. His account is competently written, but very challenging nonetheless. Careful analysis of the culture at this time sheds light on a sexist and misogynistic undertone lurking beneath the truest facts of this case, and I do believe that if the same thing were to happen today, with proper advances in medicine, psychotherapy, politics, and law, that such a strange and sordid circus would not be allowed to leave the ground, and those innocents who had been hurt and abused by such crimes would see true justice. As difficult as it is to read, I was very thankful to read it with the amazing Sveta, and I do consider it important material for those researching United States law or mental health issues, or those looking for various and high profile true crime stories of historical significance. To add to the overall strangeness of this whole affair, both Milligan and Keyes passed away in 2014. A follow up book, called The Milligan Wars is yet to be published here in the US, despite being published overseas (in countries such as Japan as early as 1994) due to Milligan’s own lawsuit against the state of Ohio! For of all things, mistreatment! I do wonder how acquittal of 3 counts of violent crime constitutes any form of mistreatment! Again, it is impossible to view this positively, unless we can hope a case like this brings about a better life for those in the future and great social changes. It is my hope that the women victimized by Milligan were able to live healthy, happy lives, because this book and this account did nothing to help them or to heal their hearts or lives, and I truly hope this book not do them even more harm than they already received at Milligan’s hand. Read this by yourself at your own risk, read it in class or a place of study, or read it with someone you love and trust because it is a very difficult subject and certainly provides food for thought.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4470839396905378678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1877813478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1877813478" />
    <a title="Johara " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4184297-johara"><img alt="Johara " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605868397p2/4184297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1877813478?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johara " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johara " href="/user/show/4184297-johara">Johara </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/34091850-the-minds-of-billy-milligan">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1877813478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12209924666676311648"> <a href='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Milligan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Billy Milligan</a>… what an extraordinary person that not only made people experience what great length the mind can go, and how fragile the person can be!!!<br/><br/>The Minds of Billy Milligan is a non-fiction book about Billy Milligan, a man with multiple-personality disorder, who was charged with different crimes and was eventually acquitted, written Daniel Keyes, a psychology graduate, who interviewed Milligan during his treatment and conferred with his carers.<br/><br/>This is not your typical non-fiction, and i</span>
  <span id="freeText12209924666676311648" style="display:none"> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Milligan" rel="nofollow noopener">Billy Milligan</a>… what an extraordinary person that not only made people experience what great length the mind can go, and how fragile the person can be!!!<br /><br />The Minds of Billy Milligan is a non-fiction book about Billy Milligan, a man with multiple-personality disorder, who was charged with different crimes and was eventually acquitted, written Daniel Keyes, a psychology graduate, who interviewed Milligan during his treatment and conferred with his carers.<br /><br />This is not your typical non-fiction, and it’s not too scientific for anyone’s liking. It’s about a guy who has 24 separate and distinct personalities, with their own different backgrounds, gender, sexual orientation, age, and accents!!! There is a long list of the personalities at the beginning of the book that you can refer back to, but the writing is done so well, that you truly experience each personality on its own, and you will come to know who is who with time. It all felt so real, so personal, so challenging at times, you just want to reach out and help Milligan.<br /><br />It also shows you how, even in the world of psychology &amp; society, multiple-personality disorder was still a controversial field that took years and years of practice and believes that it is real, and people can get help for it.<br /><br />There is also the horror of how Milligan had to deal with all the blackouts, memory losses, and being charged for crimes he has no recollection of.. because they were done by someone else!!! And then when it’s revealed later which personality was responsible…… oh my goodness the climax you get out of this story!!!! And don’t get me started on Milligan’s consciousness, or “on the spot”. The mind is truly a mystery!<br /><br />Yes it’s non-fiction, but this will be a non-fiction that you’ve never read before. It’s a rollercoaster ride of the mind, and how far it can go!!! And Keyes was so good in capturing all these moments, all these experiences, he will make you see it, feel it, and hear it.<br /><br />This is by far the best non-fiction I have read, and probably the only one I will ever recommend, if you want to challenge your mind.<br /><br />This is an interesting site that I found that has many pictures of Billy Milligan that is worth checking: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.dispatch.com">https://www.dispatch.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12209924666676311648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1538458552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1538458552" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51698221-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454186431p2/51698221.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1538458552?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/51698221-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1538458552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16269296697794940852"> Have you ever wanted to meet any literature character? <br/><br/> I guess everyone has. There is a number of people I would really pull out of pages too. And after reading a book about a man with 24 separate personalities including, for example, a colour-blind Yugoslavian 'keeper of hate', a lesbian who raped women, a drug-addicted and several other bright, independent and sometimes totally different alters, there is a new leader in this list. And the fact that Billy Milligan was a real person, the first</span>
  <span id="freeText16269296697794940852" style="display:none"> Have you ever wanted to meet any literature character? <br /><br /> I guess everyone has. There is a number of people I would really pull out of pages too. And after reading a book about a man with 24 separate personalities including, for example, a colour-blind Yugoslavian 'keeper of hate', a lesbian who raped women, a drug-addicted and several other bright, independent and sometimes totally different alters, there is a new leader in this list. And the fact that Billy Milligan was a real person, the first DID patient who successfully used his diagnosis as a defense at court, makes it truly catching.<br /> "The minds of Billy Milligan' is not the first book where I meet a man with multiple personalities. What is more, since teenage years the Narrator and Tyler Durden have been my favourite psychos :) So there is no wonder that most probably it will be found on a "favourites" bookshelf. <br /> The most curious thing for me there is how Billy’s alters shared their "duties" - someone was responsible for artistic talents, another kept a good shape, the third kept pain, cooked etc. But the one who attracted me most of all is an Englishman Arthur, a man of great intelligence, educated in many spheres such as medicine and sciences at all, who learned languages by himself. It was he who made the others “… never be still, never waste time, never allow their minds to stagnate.” (Can I have such Arthur in my head too?)<br /><br /> For those who prefer deep metaphors, colourful descriptions and rich language there is a huge disappointment - mostly it is a biography with dry facts written in order to introduce us Billy Milligan but let it be no detraction from the work the author made. I guess it was not an easy task to get closer to all his personalities as changes between them took place instantly and nobody knew what to expect.<br /> This book is one of the cases when you regret that there are only 600 pages but not 1200 and after finishing it you just stare at the ceiling wondering what was really happening in Billy's head and how the story finished (Billy Milligan died at the age of 59 in 2014, they say, with all personalities fused).<br /><br /> I have no idea how challenging it must be for DiCaprio who is going to play the lead role in The Crowded Room, the film based on this book but well…let’s see.<br /><br /> Incredible story. <br /> Incredible person.<br /><br /> P.S. One of the personalities was Slavic. A communist who drank vodka...khm...<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16269296697794940852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1664576095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1664576095" />
    <a title="Aya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32740224-aya"><img alt="Aya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475251203p2/32740224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1664576095?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aya" href="/user/show/32740224-aya">Aya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140172669" href="/book/show/16096185-the-minds-of-billy-milligan">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32740224-aya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32740224-aya?shelf=my-all-time-favourites">my-all-time-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1664576095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13943736309358634605">This book is what introduced me to what's commonly known as MDP-Multiple Personality Disorder (now called Dissociative Identity Disorder). It was written in 1981, a time where only a few doctors and therapists believed in MDP, where it was unlikely for Billy to recover.<br/>He was the host of 24 different personalities: men, women and children. It all started when he was a kid. Not bearing his stepfather's sexual abuse on a regular basis, Billy's mind developed another personality to suffer his pain </span>
  <span id="freeText13943736309358634605" style="display:none">This book is what introduced me to what's commonly known as MDP-Multiple Personality Disorder (now called Dissociative Identity Disorder). It was written in 1981, a time where only a few doctors and therapists believed in MDP, where it was unlikely for Billy to recover.<br />He was the host of 24 different personalities: men, women and children. It all started when he was a kid. Not bearing his stepfather's sexual abuse on a regular basis, Billy's mind developed another personality to suffer his pain . And so on, whenever Billy found himself in a situation where he would need to escape, his mind developes a personality according to Billy's needs. He ended up with 24 different 'people' inside of him. Each one with a purpose. Not all desirable. <br />He started to act weird around his friends and family, doing things and denying having done them afterwards. People would call him a liar, he wasn't even conscious of his new state. He became weaker, sank into depression and decided to kill himself. That's when one of his personalities showed up and 'put him to sleep', he was becoming a danger to all of them, threatening to kill them. The personalities took over for almost 2 years. During which the undesirables commited crimes, the most serious one being rape. He got arrested, pleaded not guilty by reason of insanity, and for the first time in history, he was discharged and sent to Hospital for treatement. <br />This book unveils one of the many mysteries of our brains. How little control we have over our body and mind, and sheds light on an important point: how our acts could contradict our intentions. So, do we really remain the same person under all circumstances? </span>
  <a data-text-id="13943736309358634605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1540410234" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1540410234" />
    <a title="Nika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11331650-nika"><img alt="Nika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479666918p2/11331650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540410234?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nika" href="/user/show/11331650-nika">Nika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540410234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14451766930994874034">The Minds of Billy Milligan is the most disturbing story I've ever read. Realizing that all of it is nothing but truth gives more shocker than the most perfect plot twist you can ever think of. <br/><br/>When I started reading this book, I was already familiar with Milligan's story - the first person who was not convicted for rape crimes for the reason of multiple personality. I was sure that nothing would surprise me, because I actually knew how it would end. I was dead wrong.<br/><br/>Billy's story, as his doctor</span>
  <span id="freeText14451766930994874034" style="display:none">The Minds of Billy Milligan is the most disturbing story I've ever read. Realizing that all of it is nothing but truth gives more shocker than the most perfect plot twist you can ever think of. <br /><br />When I started reading this book, I was already familiar with Milligan's story - the first person who was not convicted for rape crimes for the reason of multiple personality. I was sure that nothing would surprise me, because I actually knew how it would end. I was dead wrong.<br /><br />Billy's story, as his doctors would say, it unlike to any medical precedent. Keyes does his best to fully explore the whole brutality of Milligan's life, shattering the very core of reader's emotions. I still find it hard to believe that an actual person lived through this hell and he survived. <br /><br />While most readers might point out that there is no heroism in describing real life events without any fictional element, after 374 pages I was convinced to the contrary. The way Daniel lays out those facts helps to step by step explore Billy's character(s). Most importantly, Keyes never suggest a judgement, empathy or apathy towards main character. He just tells the story in a way that your attitude to this man, convicted with rape, changes from chapter to chapter.<br /><br />Some parts of this book I found extremely dynamic and mind blowing. First, when his lawyers started to realize that Billy has multiple personalities and second, when it described how each distinct personality emerged through time. <br /><br />There might be a lot masterpieces awaiting for me to read, but I am sure there is no story that will be so affecting emotionally or morally.<br /><br />A must read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14451766930994874034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2114510305" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2114510305" />
    <a title="Edina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46118760-edina"><img alt="Edina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503165293p2/46118760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2114510305?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edina" href="/user/show/46118760-edina">Edina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2114510305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10316347505771842972">*Incredibly unpopular opinion ahead apparently*<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>We know that a world without pain is a world without feeling...but a world without feeling is a world without pain.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>The life of Billy Milligan is as tragic as it is fascinating and the fact that this book does indeed shine a light on the traumas that he went through and that eventually led to his multiple personality disorder makes me glad that I picked it up. It's extremely heartbreaking how people at that time handled his situation, how there w</span>
  <span id="freeText10316347505771842972" style="display:none">*Incredibly unpopular opinion ahead apparently*<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>We know that a world without pain is a world without feeling...but a world without feeling is a world without pain.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The life of Billy Milligan is as tragic as it is fascinating and the fact that this book does indeed shine a light on the traumas that he went through and that eventually led to his multiple personality disorder makes me glad that I picked it up. It's extremely heartbreaking how people at that time handled his situation, how there were so many bitter people who instead of helping him by offering him as much support as they could, or at least keeping their mouth shut, decided to harm a poor soul. Of course, just as in every one of us, in Billy there were personalities or 'people' that were not the definition of a good samaritan, but they were kept in check by personalities such as Arthur's, an incredibly logical person with a deep understanding on how he should treat other people. Split as he was, Billy has always shown a desire to protect women and children from harm, something that no one has offered him as a child when faced with his stepfather's cruel and torturous actions. I'm deeply saddened by the fact that he was branded as a liar and that he didn't get all the help that he needed from those surrounding him, from people who couldn't understand one simple fact pointed out very well in the book: <i>when you were trying to help the mentally disordered, you had to put aside feelings of vengeance and deal with the individual.</i><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>We, I, am a freak, a misfit, a biological error.<br /><br /><b>Is life worth living in the jaws of society's trash can for misfit minds?</b></blockquote>
</i> <br /><br />All this said though, I was very disappointed with the way Daniel Keyes decided to write Billy's story. The way he narrates is of course very matter-of-fact, but sometimes you are reading reports and they do get very boring. Also I was irritated by the fact that he decided to mention every single person that ever came into contact with him. Just a simple list at the end (if he considered it necessary) of the personnel in the institutions that Billy ever stepped into would have sufficed. But such as it is, I was put through the ordeal of reading and memorizing names that will never help me in any way. I don't care what nurse refused to treat him at one point. I just don't.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10316347505771842972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1051154395" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1051154395" />
    <a title="Bella Baghdasaryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27652663-bella-baghdasaryan"><img alt="Bella Baghdasaryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401112156p2/27652663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1051154395?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bella Baghdasaryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bella Baghdasaryan" href="/user/show/27652663-bella-baghdasaryan">Bella Baghdasaryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27652663-bella-baghdasaryan?shelf=mind-brain">mind-brain</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1051154395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7918558289782247832"><p>
  <i>‘I don’t have problem. I am part of problem.’</i>
</p><br/>The Minds of Billy Milligan is the result of numerous interviews/discussions with Milligan (and some of his many personalities) and most of the people involved in the case, as well as interviews Keyes conducted with the people involved in Milligan’s personal life. It is always interesting to read about real people and their stories, but in a non-fiction but you are not expecting to find such a fantastic story. <br/><p>
  <b>Twenty-four people live inside Bil</b></p></span>
  <span id="freeText7918558289782247832" style="display:none"><p>
  <i>‘I don’t have problem. I am part of problem.’</i>
</p><br />The Minds of Billy Milligan is the result of numerous interviews/discussions with Milligan (and some of his many personalities) and most of the people involved in the case, as well as interviews Keyes conducted with the people involved in Milligan’s personal life. It is always interesting to read about real people and their stories, but in a non-fiction but you are not expecting to find such a fantastic story. <br /><p>
  <b>Twenty-four people live inside Billy Milligan.</b>
</p><br />David, the eight-year-old "keeper of pain"; Arthur, the Englishman; Ragen, the "keeper of Rage" who possessed incredible strength; Allen, the con man; Tommy, the escape-artist, and all of the others, including men, women, several children, both boys and girls, and the Teacher, the only one who can put them all together. Each of these "people" play a distinct role. Keyes captures this well, making it possible to clearly envision all of these people running around inside the body of one man.<br />It is an informative, thought-provoking, and well written book. It was also a good reminder of just how little we still know about how our brains function.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7918558289782247832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2079246817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_2720515385" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2720515385" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17817291-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442015982p2/17817291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2720515385?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/17817291-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17817291-tim?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17817291-tim?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17817291-tim?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17817291-tim?shelf=autobiography-biography-memoir">autobiography-biography-memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2720515385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17148778853360333396">I have read some atypical biographies in my time but this book was without a doubt the most bizarre I have ever come across. I suppose that is to be expected when the subject of the biography has twenty four different personalities: some young, some old, some male, some female, some domestic, some foreign. A few observations both about the book and about dissociative identity disorder (DID) in general:<br/><br/>1) The way the book is written suggests the author is using some degree of dramatic license. It</span>
  <span id="freeText17148778853360333396" style="display:none">I have read some atypical biographies in my time but this book was without a doubt the most bizarre I have ever come across. I suppose that is to be expected when the subject of the biography has twenty four different personalities: some young, some old, some male, some female, some domestic, some foreign. A few observations both about the book and about dissociative identity disorder (DID) in general:<br /><br />1) The way the book is written suggests the author is using some degree of dramatic license. It makes the book very readable, though one might argue not as accurate as it might be otherwise.<br /><br />2) DID is a very contested area within the psychiatric community, something I had not been aware of until a few months ago when I pulled an encyclopedia of pseudoscience off the bookshelf at a thrift store and randomly flipped it open to the entry for DID. One skeptic suggests DID should stand for dangerously inaccurate diagnosis.<br /><br />3) As someone who is interested in the relationship between the mind and the body, one of the things that fascinates me about DID are studies that appear to demonstrate that the switch from one personality to another can result in physiological changes in the body. Much like the potential readiness experiments Benjamin Libet carried out that supposedly disprove free will, these studies have both their supporters and their detractors.<br /><br />4) The alters of Billy Milligan thought of themselves as separate people rather than separate personalities. At one point in the book one of them takes offence at a doctor referring to them as personalities.<br /><br />5) Billy Milligan was a very accomplished painter. Because of this, he was able to produce realistic portraits of the different alters. Some of them are reproduced in the book. <br /><br />6) It was reading a different book by the author (referred to in the text in the third person as 'the writer' ) that convinced Billy to let him document his story. The title of that book isn't mentioned but I suspect it was probably <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36576608.Flowers_for_Algernon" title="Flowers for Algernon by Daniel Keyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Flowers for Algernon</a>.<br /><br />7) Daniel Keyes wrote a sequel to this book entitled <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2625536.The_Milligan_Wars" title="The Milligan Wars by Daniel Keyes" rel="nofollow noopener">The Milligan Wars</a> that has never been released in the United States because of a legal dispute with the state of Ohio. Unfortunately I don't speak any of the languages of the countries where it has been published. <br /><br />8) Keyes paints a sympathetic picture of Milligan that made him more a victim than a villain. It is, of course, possible that he was just a con man as some people have alleged but if so, he was an exceptionally good con man. Keeping the back stories, mannerisms, and talents of twenty four different parts you were playing straight without tripping up and fooling many people in both the psychiatric and legal community is not something that just anyone could pull off successfully. <br /><br />This was an excellent and engrossing read, though due to the nature of the subject matter I can't say it was always an enjoyable one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17148778853360333396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2009974391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2009974391" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4093195-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465667678p2/4093195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009974391?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/4093195-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9785699814398" href="/book/show/35223299">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093195-victoria?shelf=biography">biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093195-victoria?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4093195-victoria?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009974391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18109304238035386965">Even though the story is about a criminal, I think most readers will agree that you can't hate Billy or his identities/minds. Daniel Keyes has done a great job depicting Billy's life in a way that makes you feel sorry for him and everything he's been through. Given the fact that contemporary TV and Hollywood movies are full of cruelty, violence, blood, sex and all that jazz, this story wasn't surprisingly shocking, but some moments were indeed repulsive. The most infuriating characters of all we</span>
  <span id="freeText18109304238035386965" style="display:none">Even though the story is about a criminal, I think most readers will agree that you can't hate Billy or his identities/minds. Daniel Keyes has done a great job depicting Billy's life in a way that makes you feel sorry for him and everything he's been through. Given the fact that contemporary TV and Hollywood movies are full of cruelty, violence, blood, sex and all that jazz, this story wasn't surprisingly shocking, but some moments were indeed repulsive. The most infuriating characters of all were people, journalists and law enforcement institutions. We all know that the world can be blindingly judgmental and nobody wants to try to walk in someone else's shoes or at least try and empathize with others, and this story proves that point pretty well. Nobody gave a damn about how Billy became the person he was, why he raped these women, why he robbed them. The world is trained to react with feelings that are expected from you in certain situations and that's it. If you feel different, if you <i>are</i> different, you don't belong and you should be locked in a cage and denied even the least -- kind attitude and proper treatment. <br /><br />The best thing about this book is that very soon the reader starts treating all Billy's identities as separate people with different traits of character, reactions, behaviour, etc. In the middle of the story I realised that I'm asking myself "what would Ragen do in that situation?", "how would Allen react?" or "what would Arthur say?", but all those identities are a part of one single person! <br /><br />This book got me thinking that although most of us are more or less sane (I hope so), difficult situations happen to all of us. Times when we don't know what to do, what's best for us and what's best for our loved ones, and in those times we also hear voices in our heads telling us what to do. And often those voices contradict each other and we stall, we postpone making a decision. Or we make one and then change our minds. Sounds familiar? So really, how different from Billy Milligan are we? Some of us might be more alike than we want to admit, so is it really our place to judge? I don't think so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18109304238035386965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3312340455" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3312340455" />
    <a title="Terry Cornell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11712998-terry-cornell"><img alt="Terry Cornell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586739721p2/11712998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3312340455?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terry Cornell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terry Cornell" href="/user/show/11712998-terry-cornell">Terry Cornell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11712998-terry-cornell?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11712998-terry-cornell?shelf=biography">biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3312340455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer387969244219183404">I give this book written by the author of 'Flowers for Algernon' author Daniel Keyes a three and a half star rating. Instead of a work of fiction however, this is the real life story of Billy Milligan. He was the first person acquitted of his crimes by reason of insanity due to his multiple personality disorder. The first part of the book is the events leading up to Milligan's arrest, and the legal process that determined he should be treated for his disorder at a low-security psychiatric hospit</span>
  <span id="freeText387969244219183404" style="display:none">I give this book written by the author of 'Flowers for Algernon' author Daniel Keyes a three and a half star rating. Instead of a work of fiction however, this is the real life story of Billy Milligan. He was the first person acquitted of his crimes by reason of insanity due to his multiple personality disorder. The first part of the book is the events leading up to Milligan's arrest, and the legal process that determined he should be treated for his disorder at a low-security psychiatric hospital versus serving time at the state mental hospital. The second part of the book is based on the author's interviews with the 'fused' Billy Milligan while he was going through treatment, telling of the events leading up to his arrest from the perspective of most of the 24 personalities he had developed. Amazingly, this isn't as confusing as it sounds. Milligan had developed these different personalities to deal with his life after being abused by his step-father at a young age. Each personality is distinct, and has particular attributes that helped Milligan deal with life. Some personalities were children, some artists, one in particular an expert in self-defense and weapons. At first this seemed unbelievable, but as the story develops it would seem virtually impossible to fake such a thing.<br /><br />The final part of the book, is relating the legal problems that started when some community members where the low-security treatment center was located became aware of his presence in the community. Through political manipulation adverse community members managed to get him transferred to the Lima State Prison Hospital, where Milligan's treatment stopped. Through legal battles over several years he was finally returned to his original treatment program. At the conclusion of the book he was still undergoing treatment. According to Wikipedia, he did complete his treatment and was released in 1988. A really interesting read--haven't read anything quite like it since 'Sybil' several years ago. The Dr. that treated Sybil identified Milligan's disorder and helped develop his treatment plan. Good book if you're interested in how our complicated minds work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="387969244219183404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2664399093" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2664399093" />
    <a title="Nona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10860485-nona"><img alt="Nona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562666149p2/10860485.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2664399093?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nona" href="/user/show/10860485-nona">Nona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553263817" href="/book/show/112504.The_Minds_of_Billy_Milligan">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10860485-nona?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10860485-nona?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2664399093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4069186585485576971">This book contains so much useful information about human psyche.<br/>This is a true story about a very uniquely talented, clever, fragile and at the same time are impossibly strong and self-disciplined person.<br/>This is a real proof to Fraud's psychoanalysis theory, that all the mental disorders are based on traumatic events of the past. When the situation becomes unbearable for the mind to accept or deal with it's reality, it represses the traumatic event in different ways depending on a person.<br/>In thi</span>
  <span id="freeText4069186585485576971" style="display:none">This book contains so much useful information about human psyche.<br />This is a true story about a very uniquely talented, clever, fragile and at the same time are impossibly strong and self-disciplined person.<br />This is a real proof to Fraud's psychoanalysis theory, that all the mental disorders are based on traumatic events of the past. When the situation becomes unbearable for the mind to accept or deal with it's reality, it represses the traumatic event in different ways depending on a person.<br />In this case, Billy Milligan had multiple personality disorder since he was a little boy. He had very traumatic childhood, which every time drove him farther away from his core personality. That was a cause of 24 personalities birth...<br />But what amazes me the most, that according to the book, he could control some of his personalities, he could help himself in various different situations, that he could adjust his personalities according to the skills he needed to deal with the exact situation.<br />In reality, everyone had more than 24 personalities within themselves before they have become a mature, independent human beings. Because, kids sometimes act very different in a seconds, sometimes they do stupid and dangerous things, sometimes they talk more mature than we can expect, sometimes they lose themselves in a game, play make-believe games, create an imaginary friends etc... which is normal in their age. And the parents role here is so much important, to guide them, teach them the right way. As every parent is unique and they all have their different priorities on right or wrong, kids develop accordingly. And in the most difficult time is when they become teenagers. It's the breaking point for them, from kids they grow into a mature individuals, the process is painful, and frequently they don't understand themselves and their actions properly, they even become amazed of their abruptly changed angry behavior and they ask themselves: "What the hell just happened ? Why did i acted this or that way?".<br />Everyone had that moments, the inner conflicts, when they had ashamed or angry on themselves for the wrong actions. Wrong according to their views which their parents had shown to them. Going back to the main point (everyone had multiple personalities within) the important thing here is, that the time we switched to the other personality, the difference was so small and was guided by the core personality, that we remembered everything what happened during that period. Like feeling an excitement or depressive for no reason (at least non obvious to person), solving a difficult equation, saying clever or sometimes stupid things etc... The core personality was strong and present during that period. Memory is the most important thing. It reminds us about how we have changed from this person to that one. Now, imagine if the person can't remember that changes have been made? He just simply can't remember who he/she was, but knows who is he/she now?<br /><br />The writing style is excellent and the book reads very interesting and in an easy way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4069186585485576971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_674141294" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674141294" />
    <a title="Ryby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3798727-ryby"><img alt="Ryby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442656538p2/3798727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/674141294?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryby" href="/user/show/3798727-ryby">Ryby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9786028579056" href="/book/show/10674233-24-wajah-billy">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ryby by: </span>
      My sister
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer674141294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9257116656359361464">For the first time after been so long not reading a thick book, I can finish this one in only less than a week. The first night I got this novel, I didn't sleep at all. My eyes were so sleepy, yet Billy's personalities journey for seven years kept me up.<br/><br/>So, what's the good in this book? I don't know myself, though. Based on true story. The first part of the novel tells of Billy Milligan who being caught due to allegations of rape by three female students from Ohio State University. When visited </span>
  <span id="freeText9257116656359361464" style="display:none">For the first time after been so long not reading a thick book, I can finish this one in only less than a week. The first night I got this novel, I didn't sleep at all. My eyes were so sleepy, yet Billy's personalities journey for seven years kept me up.<br /><br />So, what's the good in this book? I don't know myself, though. Based on true story. The first part of the novel tells of Billy Milligan who being caught due to allegations of rape by three female students from Ohio State University. When visited by police at his apartment and questioned, Billy confessed that his name is not Billy. The police certainly do not believe and finally brought Milligan to jail. It was determined that Billy's personality, style of speech, accent, and his behavior always changing from time to time. Sometimes he spoke fluent English with an accent and haughty attitude, then seconds later turned into Serbo-Croatian accent with a defensive stance like a fighter, and then changed again into an anti-social person who hate others. When finally he was treated by a psychiatrist, only then William Stanley Milligan was diagnosed with multiple personalities. And it turns out, there are twenty-four different personalities, who live in Milligan's body.<br /><br />Twenty-four!! Can you imagine?! o.O <br /><br />These twenty four personalities were in turn controlled Billy's body, taking his consciousness, while the core personality kept asleep for seven years. This book presents the life experience of Billy Milligan during controlled by the twenty-four personalities that full of horrible stories.<br /><br />To be honest I rarely read a psychological novel based on true stories like this. My sister, who was a psychologist university student, recommend it to me because she knew I was working on a project of novel writing with the theme of split personality. I initially thought I would not finish it, look at the thickness of this novel. But it was only in less than a week I have finished. Daniel Keyes has presented the facts in a very flowing style of storytelling and firm, with no eliminating the reports, hospital diagnosis, letters, and interviews from around the Billy relatives who can help this novel. Everything was presented very neatly. Very interesting, very thrilling, and deserves five-star rating from me. ^ ^</span>
  <a data-text-id="9257116656359361464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2120859218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120859218" />
    <a title="Puja Baruah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28914027-puja-baruah"><img alt="Puja Baruah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505185982p2/28914027.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120859218?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Puja Baruah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Puja Baruah" href="/user/show/28914027-puja-baruah">Puja Baruah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120859218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12282672932827814708">Dr. George Harding noted that the fused Billy Milligan will be less than the sum of his parts. <br/><br/>This is sadly true. Through the book, the writer takes you on a journey of the life of a man and the 23 other persons that live inside him. You begin by fearing the Billy responsible for Ohio State University rapes, wishing him to go to jail. The writer skilfully introduces you to their superficial selves first; Arthur's superiority, Ragen's anger, Allen's street smartness, Adalana's sexuality and you </span>
  <span id="freeText12282672932827814708" style="display:none">Dr. George Harding noted that the fused Billy Milligan will be less than the sum of his parts. <br /><br />This is sadly true. Through the book, the writer takes you on a journey of the life of a man and the 23 other persons that live inside him. You begin by fearing the Billy responsible for Ohio State University rapes, wishing him to go to jail. The writer skilfully introduces you to their superficial selves first; Arthur's superiority, Ragen's anger, Allen's street smartness, Adalana's sexuality and you almost detest them for landing innocent unaware Billy into so much trouble. But as you uncover the motives and traits of each alter ego, you feel yourself thawing bit by bit. You find yourself respecting Arthur's need to bring order, Ragen's need to protect the younger ones, Allen's smart tongue to get out of sticky situations, Tommy's capacity to emotionally connect with others. At other times, you find yourself learning to appreciate Adalana's loneliness or Chistene's warm heart; each personality has a distinct trait and yet the red thread that ties them together is their love for art. If Arthur's system had worked, it would have been utterly cool. And yet, as it turns out- nothing is perfect. In fact, nothing is ever perfect for more than a couple of weeks and soon enough, the system breaks down; there are mix-ups and things spiral out of control. In this time of "mix up" is when Billy breaks the law. <br /><br />You will find his team of lawyers, doctors, and the writer doing everything in their power to help him. And yet, what fails Billy is the system: its bureaucracy and its ill-timed apathy. I googled what happened to Billy after the novel was published. It seems in 1988, he was finally released from his various mental hospitals but he died of cancer in 2014. The pain felt by others is unimaginable, but the writer does immense justice to Billy and the various "persons" inside him since he gave a voice to each. Despite being a Psychology student I never knew the innate workings of Split personalities as well as have been explained in this book. <br />A great read, if you are interested in Psychology or biographies.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12282672932827814708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
