<div id="review_1249008749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249008749" />
    <a title="CHERRY" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9950144-cherry"><img alt="CHERRY" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464589581p2/9950144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249008749?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CHERRY" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CHERRY" href="/user/show/9950144-cherry">CHERRY</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553263817" href="/book/show/112504.The_Minds_of_Billy_Milligan">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9950144-cherry?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249008749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16809743667838381447">My first impression of Dissociative identity disorder (DID) came from the film <i>Primal Fear</i> starring Edward Norton as a brutal murderer who pretends to have the disorder. I attempted to read this book when I was in Primary 5 but it was too difficult for me then, so my feelings toward DID remained suspicious.<br/><br/>Keyes' report of Milligan's true story made me believe. The pieces surrounding Milligan's story are gathered very well to present a smooth story. I kept finding out more about his "people" and</span>
  <span id="freeText16809743667838381447" style="display:none">My first impression of Dissociative identity disorder (DID) came from the film <i>Primal Fear</i> starring Edward Norton as a brutal murderer who pretends to have the disorder. I attempted to read this book when I was in Primary 5 but it was too difficult for me then, so my feelings toward DID remained suspicious.<br /><br />Keyes' report of Milligan's true story made me believe. The pieces surrounding Milligan's story are gathered very well to present a smooth story. I kept finding out more about his "people" and soon found myself fascinated by their existence and sympathising for their experience. Although I don't particularly favour any of the personalities, Arthur, Ragen, Allen, Tommy, and Danny stayed in me. I feel they represent parts that we all have, but we're just blessed to be able to stay fused.<br /><br />I'm glad the book includes a note on scientific discussion about brain wave activities in ordinary people and DID patients. These last pages ought to move the non-believers to "understand" and give them "the least [they] deserve".<br /><br />All contribution to this book should be appreciated for bringing an otherwise buried story to light, and for giving countless people a glimpse of the life of the many living with DID.<br /><br />I'm surely going to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/67920.Sybil_The_Classic_True_Story_of_a_Woman_Possessed_by_Sixteen_Personalities" title="Sybil The Classic True Story of a Woman Possessed by Sixteen Personalities by Flora Rheta Schreiber" rel="nofollow noopener">Sybil: The Classic True Story of a Woman Possessed by Sixteen Personalities</a> and Keyes' best-known work <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18373.Flowers_for_Algernon" title="Flowers for Algernon by Daniel Keyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Flowers for Algernon</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16809743667838381447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2865077543" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2865077543" />
    <a title="Ioana Ioana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63497622-ioana-ioana"><img alt="Ioana Ioana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590230014p2/63497622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2865077543?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ioana Ioana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ioana Ioana" href="/user/show/63497622-ioana-ioana">Ioana Ioana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9786068811079" href="/book/show/35442225-min-ile-lui-billy-milligan">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2865077543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1433111188867443026"><b> 1981, Escape valves? A transient illness?</b><br/><br/>Imaginary friends do not grow up. They are simply disposed of. They do not grow old, nor do they learn new tricks or get married. These tax exempt entities will hang around <i>only</i> for a while, you know, like...Koosalagoopagoop.<br/><br/>Imagine having 24 permanent (more or less) residents, each a personality in its own right, with their own idiosyncratic dispositions, distinctive cognitive abilities and temperaments. Not imaginary friends, symptoms.<br/>Beyond abused and</span>
  <span id="freeText1433111188867443026" style="display:none"><b> 1981, Escape valves? A transient illness?</b><br /><br />Imaginary friends do not grow up. They are simply disposed of. They do not grow old, nor do they learn new tricks or get married. These tax exempt entities will hang around <i>only</i> for a while, you know, like...Koosalagoopagoop.<br /><br />Imagine having 24 permanent (more or less) residents, each a personality in its own right, with their own idiosyncratic dispositions, distinctive cognitive abilities and temperaments. Not imaginary friends, symptoms.<br />Beyond abused and battered there’s the damage control unit which took over and gave rise to William Stanley Milligan’s multiple personalities (or well thought out performance), from a witty, snobbish “professor” -Arthur (core personality), to Samuel, an orthodox Jew, Adalana, an affection crazed lesbian, Ragen, a karate expert or Tommy, an escape artist (and more). <br />Skeptical, I ploughed through (while listening to a lot of Ween, incidentally).<br /><br />Keyes was assiduous in laying down Billy’s coming of age story, but sauntered his way to unpacking medical evidence, scarcely imparted only in a couple of pages at the end of the book and remained quiescent on addressing the biggest question of all: What is consciousness? Contrary evidence to Keyes’ belief in the diagnosis was frugally mentioned, so in lack of a fuller picture, the inference you make might be tarnished. Prevalence would be a key aspect to research. Abuse remains a hard hitting, impactful anachronistic evil.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1433111188867443026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eYFvTyZvo1Xb/4XLHugfdgY7d8gedw/0c1T2p9XyYXYSrrq0LXt35VINL6usFztYu4NWQ8U6GNTvULc3VhXhbQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11072.Daniel_Keyes">About Daniel Keyes</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/11072.Daniel_Keyes"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1328430586p3/11072.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12486380280846832930">Daniel Keyes was an American author best known for his Hugo award-winning short story and Nebula award-winning novel <i>Flowers for Algernon</i>. Keyes was given the Author Emeritus honor by the Science Fiction and Fantasy Writers of America in 2000.<br/><br/>Keyes was born in Brooklyn, New York City, New York. At age 17, he joined the U.S. Maritime Service as ship's purser. He obtained a B.A. in psychology from B</span>
  <span id="freeText12486380280846832930" style="display:none">Daniel Keyes was an American author best known for his Hugo award-winning short story and Nebula award-winning novel <i>Flowers for Algernon</i>. Keyes was given the Author Emeritus honor by the Science Fiction and Fantasy Writers of America in 2000.<br /><br />Keyes was born in Brooklyn, New York City, New York. At age 17, he joined the U.S. Maritime Service as ship's purser. He obtained a B.A. in psychology from Brooklyn College, and after a stint in fashion photography (partner in a photography studio), earned a Master's Degree in English and American Literature at night while teaching English in New York City public schools during the day and writing weekends.<br /><br />In the early 1950s, he was editor of the pulp magazine <i>Marvel Science Fiction</i> for publisher Martin Goodman. Circa 1952, Keyes was one of several staff writers, officially titled editors, who wrote for such horror and science fiction comics as <i>Journey into Unknown Worlds</i>, for which Keyes wrote two stories with artist Basil Wolverton. From 1955-56, Keyes wrote for the celebrated EC Comics, including its titles <i>Shock Illustrated</i> and <i>Confessions Illustrated</i>, under both his own name and the pseudonyms Kris Daniels, A.D. Locke and Dominik Georg.<br /><br />The short story and subsequent novel, <i>Flowers for Algernon</i>, is written as progress reports of a mentally disabled man, Charlie, who undergoes experimental surgery and briefly becomes a genius before the effects tragically wear off. The story was initially published in the April 1959 issue of <i>The Magazine of Fantasy &amp; Science Fiction</i> and the expanded novel in 1966. The novel has been adapted several times for other media, most prominently as the 1968 film <i>Charly</i>, starring Cliff Robertson (who won an Academy Award for Best Actor) and Claire Bloom. He also won the Hugo Award in 1959 and the Nebula Award in 1966.<br /><br />Keyes went on to teach creative writing at Wayne State University, and in 1966 he became an English and creative writing professor at Ohio University, in Athens, Ohio, where he was honored as a professor emeritus in 2000.<br /><br />Keyes' other books include <i>The Fifth Sally, The Minds of Billy Milligan, The Touch, Unveiling Claudia</i>, and the memoir<i> Algernon, Charlie, and I: A Writer's Journey</i>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12486380280846832930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_41563725'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41563725?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Війни Міллігана<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/11072.Daniel_Keyes?origin=series_works\">Daniel Keyes<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.98 avg rating &mdash; 408 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1994\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer14175042844569611690\">Коли здавалося, що всі неприємності вже позаду, життя кидає Біллі нове випробування. На нього чекає курс лікування у психіатричній клініці для злочинців у Лімі. Це місце вважалося справдешнім пеклом на землі. Те, що коїли з пацієнтами у цих стінах, м<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14175042844569611690\" style=\"display:none\">Коли здавалося, що всі неприємності вже позаду, життя кидає Біллі нове випробування. На нього чекає курс лікування у психіатричній клініці для злочинців у Лімі. Це місце вважалося справдешнім пеклом на землі. Те, що коїли з пацієнтами у цих стінах, мало залишатися моторошною таємницею. І побиття та щоденні знущання було далеко не найжахливішим з того, що чекало тут на Біллі. Але він не такий, як інші хворі. Він має 24 особистості та безмежну волю до життя. У голові Біллі точаться запеклі війни, і його намагатимуться знищити, не розуміючи, що мають справу не з ним одним… Яка боротьба буде простішою — із системою чи із самим собою?<\/span>\n  <a
